User_8e115b: We get CPT. You do need an offer to apply for cpt but it is fairly quick&all online
User_8e115b: The job needs to be related to your major though
User_8e115b: For the fields in job application that asks if you need sponsorship you do NOT need it. As its kinda self-sponsored through minerva
User_8e115b: After graduation we get OPT which is similar but takes a bit more effort. Still you cab safely put "no" in the sponsorship field of job applications

--- Conversation 6 (2023-01-14) ---
User_4e0cf1: Hello. I am looking for internships, and I have a question. Do I need to get a transcript per application? Meaning that the "recipient" in the official transcript request should be changed every time.
User_a591e3: Do they require an official one? Most I've seen let you send in an unofficial one. If they do require it, some ask you to send it and some ask the school to. If you can send it, have the official one sent to you and then you can send it to multiple. If it does require it from the school, then yes, you have to change the recipient
User_4e0cf1: If I upload the unofficial one, how do I show the GPA (it is required)?
User_c177ea: You can merge pdfs (I’m assuming you’re a freshman and you don’t get a Gpa on your unofficial transcript)

It's that time of the semester where we're making summer plans and working towards getting internships. A great way to boost your resume is to do a Paragon One externship. It's a 10-hr/week commitment and gives you insight into what working in a certain field looks like. Below is a list of externships that have my referral link and at the bottom is a general link to all the externships. 

Feel free to message me if you have any questions!

--- Conversation 20 (2023-01-31) ---
User_e118cc: Thanks Atahan! Is it the same if the question asks whether we will ever need visa sponsorship?
User_b6cf6b: yes
User_8e115b: you can also think of it this way: if you say you do need a sponsorship then a bot will reject you. If you say you dont (and really you dont need for a good while) then you might get selected against when a human person learns that you are on OPT/CPT (because they will learn at some point). Also what if you marry in your 3 years and now dont need a visa? who knows if you will work there for 3 years in this job market?

The only thing that matters is that you can say you dont need a visa at this very moment. And saying you dont need a visa increases your chances of getting the job.

--- Conversation 31 (2023-02-14) ---
User_f39ece: Hello! Does anyone know how to convert GPA from Minerva grades to the standard system? Or do we have to request this from Minerva?
User_bb0394: min/max scores refer to the score you see in your Outcome Index (average of your LO scores), and if your grade falls somewhere between 3.35 and 3.55, your letter score is A-. Then you look at the second table and see that for A-, your GPA would be 3.7
User_bb0394: Conclusion: if you want to keep your GPA equal/above 3.7, try to get min 3.35 in all your courses :)
User_bb0394: u can ask registrar for it too if u want, but i think most of us just convert it ourselves

User_455221: TL:DR; Summer Opportunity, Apply Here

 (https://ixlink.co/juliet-m37)Hi everyone, My name is Juliet, studying Arts and Humanities. For those still looking for summer plans, applications are closing this week iX Summer, a program in which you take a career-focused course in a city abroad (Lisbon or Cape Town). The program includes a 4-week internship project in collaboration with local firms, which you can put on your resume. Courses are offered in the following fields:

Investment Finance | Management Consulting | Data Science & AI | Software Engineering

This is perfect for first-years and sophomores looking to go abroad and start accumulating experience for future recruiting sessions. I participated in the program remotely and had the best time. iXperience has had thousands of alumni from Harvard, Princeton, Penn, Duke, UVA, Michigan, and more. I'm happy to talk about my experience if you are interested, just drop me an email.

The final deadline to apply is Thursday Feb 16 at 11:59pm PT.

Applications (click here) (https://ixlink.co/juliet-m37) are free and non-binding. Financial aid is also available.

Best regards,

Juliet Mwaniki

User_d443af: Hey guys, how are you?

MCC Corps Leaders = June 20th – August 25th, 10 weeks, $25/hour, 40 hours/week, 2 positions (1 Boston, 1 North Shore)

MCC Corps Members = June 26th – August 18th, 8 weeks, $18-20/hour, 30-35 hours/week, 8 positions (4 Boston, 4 North Shore)

 

There will be 2 MCC program hubs in 2023 – one in Boston at the Boston Nature Center, and one in the North Shore at Joppa Flats in Newburyport.

User_f0e085: Did anyone have to do FBI Fingerprint Clearance for an internship? Want to ask a question
User_89d1c4: Did any upperclassmen go through IB recruitment in London? Is it even possible? Would love to ask some questions if someone had the exposure
User_e0d81f: Yeah I'm going through it right now, it's quite simple
User_f0e085: Long shot but is there a way to do it without being in the states that's fast? I need to do it asap and mailing my fingerprints from India will take at least 20 days and I'll be in the US by then anyways.
User_e0d81f: The instructions packet I got says that I can only provide my fingerprints while being physically present in the US, and that any fingerprint cards sent from abroad won't be processed. Apparently that's a requirement from the FBI and not from the company that's processing my background check.

I told them that I'm not in the US at the moment and they told me to just go to an UPS location before starting my internship to get my fingerprints scanned. It could even be the same day I'm starting as long as I do it before I get to the office.

The packet says that processing usually takes just a few minutes and results are immediately available online. I'm not sure if all background check agencies work the same way though.
User_f0e085: That makes sense. I think the only option is to do it asap once I arrive in the US. Thank youuuuu Lucas!!

User_792c42: Hi upperclassmen who did the Roote fellowship; would love to learn about your experience - particularly if you felt any growth and had any goals/expectations you went with which were/not accomplished. Thanks!
User_a56433: I did the Roote fellowship last summer, so things are likely a bit different since then as they like to improve stuff with each iteration. 

Personally, I found that Roote was extremely beneficial because of the people who are part of Roote. Being connected to Rhys, the one who leads Roote, is perhaps the main benefit I had from the fellowship. He was extremely helpful throughout fellowship (sometimes gives me Prof Powers vibes) and also after, as you kinda have access to him and the other Roote community even after the fellowship. So, while the actual curriculum that is taught and the experience of building something during the fellowship was quite decent (wherein I learned about ideas such as agency and more about systems thinking beyond the Complex Systems class), I'm most grateful for the connections I made during it. So, I would recommend!

User_51212c: Forwarding this on behalf of the Institute of Singapore Chartered Accountants (ISCA) - 
 
We are excited to share with you about ISCA’s inaugural Global Talent Programme (GTP) (https://isca.org.sg/GTP) and would like to invite accountancy and non-accountancy undergraduates to participate in the programme. This programme would be a unique learning and networking opportunity as all participants will gather in Singapore for a fully paid-for industry learning experience.
 
To date, we have over 1,300 applicants from 44 different nationalities eager to be part of the GTP. Participating students will enjoy a fully funded accommodation stay together in Singapore, including local undergraduates, creating a great opportunity for cross-cultural connections!
 
About ISCA’s Global Talent Programme
ISCA is hosting a 1-week immersion experience from 22 July to 26 July 2024 for undergraduates (from any discipline) from all around the globe to gain new perspectives on Singapore and the abundant career opportunities within the accountancy sector. During the programme, they will get the opportunity to:
 
 1 Engage and network with industry stakeholders and experienced professionals during visits to Singapore corporations, major accounting firms and government agencies.
 2 Learn technical skills from their mentors and peers as they tackle problem statements concerning the accountancy sector.
 
The programme will provide the students with opportunities to experience Singapore’s dynamic business environment, develop a global perspective and build their leadership, communication and project management skills. The students will gain an understanding of opportunities in the accountancy sector, especially the high-growth areas in Singapore’s vibrant business ecosystem.
 
Participating students will not need to pay for any expenses from the programme.
 
Pre-requisites for applicants
 • Current undergraduate university student (from any discipline, not limited to accountancy)
 • Good command of English (e.g General Paper C, IELTS 6 or TOEFL iBT 85 or SAT Evidence-Based Reading and Writing score of 500 or AP English Language Grade 3)
 • Strong interest in the accountancy sector or business corporations
 
Register now at https://isca.org.sg/gtp (https://isca.org.sg/gtp). (https://isca.org.sg/gtp) Application closes on 4 March 2024, Monday.
 
This is a great opportunity for undergraduates from all over the world to learn from each other!

User_293f28: For M27 women interested in finance/business/real estate/VC or anything related:

Deadline: Oct 15

I would highly recommend applying to Girls Who Invest! It's a fully funded program that matches you with an internship for your sophomore summer and gives you a huge support system + network of other girls from other schools. 

They have the summer intensive program (https://www.girlswhoinvest.org/sip), where you spend the month of June learning about finance with other scholars. Then, all scholars are guaranteed to be matched with an internship across the US for July and August.

I don't know too much about the online intensive program (https://www.girlswhoinvest.org/oip), but participating in it still gives you access to the entire GWI portal and a ton of job opportunities.

This program really changed my life and I can't recommend it enough. Ik some of you already applied, but feel free to reach out to me if you have any more questions about it :)

Application Link (https://apply.girlswhoinvest.org/register/?id=22cc678f-6ac9-4c61-b935-c9a5775d6130)

User_1cd992: Tbf it’s in the best interest of America to optimize their systems for Americans so that part of it makes sense. F1 visa is built on the premise of you going back to your home country anyways, but sometimes it’s difficult for people in our positions to go back because of the economy, politics, loan commitments, etc. 

And for Tjalling to say “apply to a job opportunity is based on racial factors bc of the inequalities overall society creates” is extremely ignorant - and maybe next time try to understand why that might be the case. A freshman/sophomore program or even an internship is nothing in the context of a 30-40 year career and so I guess it’s more a privilege to underrepresented groups that such programs exist than it is a disservice to traditionally more represented groups that they are there - there’s still larger fractions of those people in those same organizations and that trend is only going to continue. At the same time, I get that it’s hard to think about careers as things we’ll do for 40 years and so crying about what you perceive as being unfair makes sense right now. But next time, please think of it as leveling the playing field - which is almost impossible anyways.     And Adam - I guess your message is also reinforcing this bad behavior, though at this point 🤷🏽‍♂️. People shouldn’t keep quiet when someone says something wrong - we should be comfortable enough to call them out & voice out our opinions and if the ways in which we do that don’t align with your values just say that not send a message to guilt trip us, being able to call out people and debate is important in any functional society - though, I do agree the manner in which you do it is just as important. But when it’s extremely inconsiderate and doesn’t take into account the make up of the group - people can’t help but get triggered thus the responses. Hard to be considerate, when someone wasn’t considerate.

--- Conversation 467 (2024-10-25) ---
User_562584: Even as an American citizen, I’ve been told outright by a gov contractor recruiter I will never get security clearance because of my association with Minerva LOL. 

There are a lot of CS jobs in the US (esp in Colorado where I’m from) that are for government contractors that work with military data that you need a security clearance for (think Lockhead Martin, Palantir, etc). Essentially, they want born and raised US citizens with little to no association with people from other countries (especially certain countries lol). 

I wouldn’t waste your time applying to anything that needs security clearance. But, there are companies (ie Palantir) that have a corporate branch (working for companies) and a government branch. You don’t need a SC for the business stuff, so you can always look for openings at the same company but on a non-goverment team!

User_74cce8: FOR 1-3 YEAR STUDENTS

The Data Science Institute Summer Lab program (launched in 2018 as the Data & Computing Summer Lab) is an immersive 8-week paid summer research program at the University of Chicago. In the program, undergraduate students (and Chicago-area high school students) are paired with data science mentors in various domains, including computer science, data science, social science, climate and energy policy, public policy, materials science, and biomedical research. Through this pairing the research assistant will engage with and hone their skills in research methodologies, practices, and teamwork. We encourage participation from a broad range of students, and require no prior research experience to apply.

https://datascience.uchicago.edu/education/summerlab/program-details/

User_74cce8: A Research Experience for Undergraduate Students

Program Details
Begins: Jun 01 2025
Ends: Aug 09 2025

Application deadline: Jan 14, 2025.

The SFI Undergraduate Complexity Research (UCR) program is a 10-week residential experience in complexity science research. Students can select from a menu of projects, or develop a project in collaboration with their mentor(s). Students learn how to combine theory, methods, and data from the physical, natural, and social sciences to ask big questions about real-world complex systems using the rigorous methods employed at SFI. Through a series of seminars and workshops, students enhance their skills as researchers and prepare for the next steps in their academic and professional journeys. 

There is no tuition for this program. 

Students receive a stipend of $700 per week, or $7,000 over the course of the program. All UCRs are provided with housing and meals at no cost to them and travel support to/from Santa Fe, New Mexico.

https://www.santafe.edu/engage/learn/programs/undergraduate-complexity-research

Today (September 19th), the application for the Cato Institute’s Spring 2026 Internship (late January–late April) just opened. The deadline is November 2, 2025.

This might not apply to most current students (especially those on visas who can’t take a leave of absence in the US), but it could be a great fit for recent graduates who want to explore opportunities after finishing their degree. Of course, check your own circumstances to see if it’s possible.

I interned at Cato in 2022, and it was a fantastic experience. Don’t buy into the idea that all young people think the same way you see in echo chambers — they don’t. One of the best parts of living in DC is the challenge of engaging seriously with people who see the world differently. On July 4th you might find yourself at a picnic with Democrats, Republicans, Progressives, MAGAs, Libertarians, and more — and still survive the fireworks together after praying and giving thanks for the food. Been there, done that.

The internship is highly competitive, but the payoff is being surrounded by sharp, driven peers. Plot twist: even among libertarian-leaning people, debates never stop! While there’s a shared foundation of values, disagreements on plenty of issues keep the challenging conversations alive.

And surprisingly, multiple interns (and even Research Assistants) I know have been accepted after openly stating they weren’t libertarians. What matters most, especially for the internship, is curiosity and a willingness to engage.

If you’re interested in exploring the ideas of Individual Liberty, Free Markets, Limited Government, and Peace, this internship is worth looking into. These ideas have shaped not only the United States, but much of Western civilization and the modern world — and they’re worth continuing to explore and fight for.

User_11d9d9: Registration for Acton University 2026 opened this month!

Acton University 2025 was the best conference I have ever attended. With 80+ countries represented and 80+ courses available, you'll feel like you'd wish you have a Time-Turner to be able to attend more lectures and meet more people.

Given the diversity of this group, I want to note the conference is very ecumenical and interfaith, inviting speakers from a variety of faith traditions like Catholicism, Protestantism, and Islam. Muslim scholars like Mustafa Akyol (Cato Institute) are recurrent speakers, and there are optional daily services for the various faith traditions represented throughout the 4-day conference — I attended some of the Catholic Masses at ~6:30am sharp ☀️. I noticed these folks take their faith seriously, haha.

TL;DR: If you take both Liberty & Natural Law seriously, definitely check out the Acton Institute—it is your intellectual home.

From their website (emphasis mine):

Acton University is not your typical conference. It’s a four-day exploration of theology, philosophy, entrepreneurship, international development, and market-based economics. Each day is packed with thought-provoking presentations on the intellectual and practical foundations of a free society. Bringing together leaders from all over the world in business and the church, academia and the ministry, the developing and developed world, and students of all ages, Acton University is a conference dedicated to connecting moral and religious principles to economic and personal liberty.

https://youtube.com/shorts/Fk8d7wDhjXA

User_11d9d9: If you support both freedom of movement and free-markets, the Cato Institute is seeking a quantitative Research Associate to join a team of data-savvy researchers working on immigration policy.

https://recruiting.paylocity.com/Recruiting/Jobs/Details/3615362

They’re looking for the kind of interdisciplinary skill set Minerva new graduates and alumni tend to have: experience with at least two data-analysis tools or programming languages (Excel, Stata, R, Python, MATLAB, etc.), and ideally some familiarity with modern econometric approaches like multiple regression, synthetic controls, difference-in-differences, and related quasi-experimental methods.

Cato's vision is to create free, open, and civil societies founded on libertarian principles. They believe that a more open legal immigration system would make America a freer, wealthier, and more prosperous country.

Very few organizations today combine and defend those ideals unapologetically, making the Cato Institute quite unique among think tanks across the political spectrum.

P.S. I’m not currently affiliated with Cato, but in 2023 I worked with their immigration team as a contractor to build the Green Card Game — https://youtu.be/haURM3eoMiI (https://youtu.be/haURM3eoMiI)

User_11d9d9: Happy New Year! 🎊🎉

The Mont Pelerin Society (MPS) invites submissions for the 2026 Hayek Essay Contest, hosted in conjunction with its 2026 Biennial Congress and General Meeting, October 11-15, 2026 in Indianapolis, Indiana, USA.

https://montpelerin.org/2026-hayek-essay-contest/

My favorite course ever at Minerva was SS166—Designing Constitutions—and I highly recommend reading The Constitution of Liberty by F.A. Hayek if you're into that stuff.

Essays should address one or more of the quotes from Hayek and/or the questions on the website.

Here's an example of the quotes you can address for your essay from The Constitution of Liberty:
“The conception of a higher law governing current legislation is a very old one. In the eighteenth century it was usually conceived as the law of God, or that of Nature, or that of Reason. But the idea of making this higher law explicit and enforceable by putting it on paper, though not entirely new, was for the first time put into practice by the Revolutionary colonists.”
– Hayek, Friedrich (1960, 2011) The Constitution of Liberty. University of Chicago Press. p. 266

User_52ac9c: 🎉The "Fundraising & Scholarship Resources for Minervans" is out!🤩

Hey everyone! 👋

Did you know? Every year, students on high financial aid struggle to afford college because of costs that aren’t fully covered, such as flights, visas, or unexpected living expenses. This is especially tough for students on maximum financial aid, whose needs often exceed what universities can offer. Just to give an idea of how problematic this is, some households aren't even able to afford the enrollment fee just to secure enrollment. As a result, many students are faced with the need to seek external funding to enroll (or stay enrolled).

The problem? There are very few practical resources that explain how to do personal fundraising effectively. Most online content focuses on NGO or startup fundraising (such as crowdfunding), but when it comes to personal fundraising campaigns (for individuals), existing resources often don't go beyond the very basics.

That’s why I built the Fundraising & Scholarship Resources for Minervans, based on insights from real fundraising experiences and analyses of successful (and unsuccessful) campaigns, to help empower students to navigate and overcome financial barriers to quality education by offering practical fundraising guidance and scholarship resources. 

Earlier versions of this guide have already been used by students from the classes of 2028 & 2029, some of which ran fundraising campaigns to come to Minerva, and I’m now sharing a more complete version with everyone.

⭐️ Access the guide here: https://fundraising101.notion.site

In this resource you will find:
• A step-by-step personal fundraising guide with actionable recommendations and insights
• A scholarship list with opportunities from organizations around the world, sorted by nationality
• [coming soon...] Additional resources to improve your fundraising campaign and to help you prepare for scholarship application processes

Read it. Use it. Help improve it. Share it.

💌 Your feedback helps strengthen bridges to education
Your unique perspective is ✨GOLD✨, especially now in the first public version of this resource! Please consider answering an anonymous feedback form - your answers directly help improve the guide and make it more useful for everyone. By taking a few minutes to respond, you’re helping make access to education more equitable 🎓💛

📝 Anonymous feedback form: https://forms.gle/oPYUFUvkZdovCFMu6

🤝 Access to education is built together
Did you know that the scholarship list is a community-built resource? Most scholarships listed came from Minervans just like you!
If you know of any scholarships that should be added to the list, you can submit them here:

➕ Scholarship submission form: https://forms.gle/PUby6PwASiFSCkB67

Or feel free to DM me scholarship names directly on Telegram if you prefer!

Together, we can help make access to college more equitable ❤️

User_09dde9: TLDR: Humans of Minerva is hiring for 3 roles this spring - all years, levels, passion are warmly welcomed with love. alums are also welcomed!! Read the full descriptions and apply below. Also come find us on Spotify and Instagram, and DM Linda if you want to be interviewed. 🎙

✍️ Narrative Designer (role we need the most, flexible timing, ~2.5-3h an episode, 2-4 episodes a sem ) → https://forms.gle/NVyRkPkWJuod7z6L7
🎤 Podcast Producer (~15–20 hours per semester. High autonomy, high reward) → https://forms.gle/iqLkyqXN7FnZftxL7
📣 Brand & Community Specialist (~1-2hours per week depends on experience, you get quicker).→ https://forms.gle/KoN4rxEiRBLPv4VH9

-—————————————————————————-
For those of you who want the full story - keep reading. 👇

Humans of Minerva started because we believed that every single person in this community has a story worth telling. Look around, do you really know your classmate, your prof, your SLT stars, and forum profiles that you see everyday in class? Do you know a memory that make them smile, an important mentor that shaped who they are, or why they keep running aside you? Do you know their word of the year, and what their tattoos could mean, and the love that they grew up with?  We sit down with them, and invite them to share their life stories and archive them because we can't all fit into a Minerva Talk at the small res halls we have.  

We've published 133 episodes so far. We've recorded 150. Across more than 50 cities, across four years, across every cohort that has ever passed through Minerva - we've been  doing the work of making sure those stories don't disappear. 

And we think this matters now more than ever. We live in a moment where AI can generate text, images, music, and voices faster than any of us can keep up with. But it cannot sit with another person, ask the right question at the right moment, and make them feel safe enough to share thoughts and stories they never had the space to share out loud. That's what we do. That's what our hosts do, what our editors do, what our whole team does - and that skill, the ability to hold space for a human story and turn it into something beautiful, is one of the most valuable things you can learn right now.

We're restructuring this spring, and we need to grow. We're looking for three people to join the team:

✍️ Narrative Designer - this is the role we need the most, and honestly, the one most people don't realize they'd be good at. You take a raw conversation and shape it into something that people actually want to listen to. No prior experience needed — just good instincts and reliability. Read the full description, it'll make you want to apply.
👉 https://forms.gle/NVyRkPkWJuod7z6L7

🎤 Podcast Producer - the full experience. You'll interview guests, shape narratives, and learn what it feels like to help someone tell the story of their own life. Read the description for the full picture.
👉 https://forms.gle/WYm1xrzRhDXnrFYp8

--- Conversation 924 (2026-03-01) ---
User_11d9d9: I wanted to share a few opportunities in the startup world that could be relevant for anyone exploring entrepreneurship.

One major one is Founder University (https://founder.university), run by the LAUNCH team. It’s a pre-accelerator program I participated in during 2024. Although my project didn’t ultimately receive funding, the experience was genuinely worthwhile because of the quality of the investors involved, what they teach, and the strength of the founder community.

The next cohort starts March 16–17, and they’re still accepting applications.

LAUNCH also invests $25,000 to $125,000 in select Founder University graduates, which makes it a meaningful on-ramp into the broader LAUNCH ecosystem.

This year they launched a Tokyo cohort as well (https://www.tokyo.launch.co), which could be especially relevant for Minerva students based there.

What stood out to me most is the philosophy of the LAUNCH team. They are unusually supportive of founders long term. They understand that ideas evolve, that first projects often don’t work, and that entrepreneurship is iterative. You’re encouraged to keep them updated, pivot if needed, and even return in future seasons with a new project. The community channels remain open — it’s not a one-and-done experience.

The program is essentially free. There’s a $500 fee, fully refunded upon completion (historically around a 95% completion rate).

I also came away with a very strong impression of Jason Calacanis. He shared that the goal of the program is for founders to remember the LAUNCH team not when everything is going well, but when things are hard — maybe even by the time they’re building their fourth startup.

Separately, LAUNCH Festival in San Francisco is also happening March 16–17. It’s capped at 400 attendees and free for early-stage founders (there’s a $10 application fee, fully refunded if you’re not approved or when you check in).

If you’re considering building something (even if you’re not sure your current idea is “the one”), I think it's a solid ecosystem.
User_11d9d9: TL; DR; Apply to the cohort 12 of Founder University here: https://founder.university/
User_11d9d9: TL; DR; If you're interested in the Tokyo version of the accelerator, check this link: https://www.tokyo.launch.co/
User_11d9d9: TL; DR; Apply to attend (or demo live at) LAUNCH FEST 2026 here: https://www.launchfestival.com/

User_11d9d9: Better late than never!

The Summer Hazlitt Fellowship by Foundation for Economic Education (FEE) has extended its deadline to April 13, so there’s still time to apply.

Last November, I shared this same opportunity for the Winter/Spring cohort, and I was glad to see someone from our community get in.

I asked her about the experience, and here’s a quick snapshot:

- You meet twice a week (lecture + workshop/guest speakers)
- Strong lineup of speakers and connections
- Cohort is quite diverse (many young professionals, some international)
- Hands-on exposure to different media formats (writing, YouTube, etc.)
- Clear libertarian lens (as expected), so it helps to stay thoughtful and critical (not a problem for Minerva students & alumni accustomed to Socratic seminars 😉!)

Overall, I hope it can be a valuable program if you're interested in economics, public policy, and modern content creation. I know people who work and have worked at FEE and can speak to their work ethic and the quality of what they produce.

For the summer cohort, the main details:

- $3,000 stipend
- 3-month program (May–August)
- Remote sessions + 5-day in-person summit (University of Maryland, expenses covered)
- Build a portfolio across formats (articles, video, podcasts, etc.)
- Mentorship + strong alumni network (Brookings, Mercatus, AEI, major media)
- Time commitment is about 8–10 hours/week, so it’s quite manageable alongside studies or work.

If this is your space, I think it's worth considering.

More details and application: https://fee.org/hazlitt-fellowship/

User_3b5692: 🪬A mysterious open call
Yesterday I visited a friend’s art studio, and I was genuinely shaken. It felt like accidentally stepping into the tomb of an ancient high civilization.
He is already a respected artist in China, but his current ambitions are not supported by the Chinese culture market. He has spent more than ten years studying Eastern metaphysics, ancient astronomy, and primordial history, all for one reason: to bring the wisdom system of ancient China back to the world stage, alongside civilizations like Egypt and the Maya.
His work carries an elegant imagination and an abyss-like sense of mystery. He has already held exhibitions across China, large and small, and people approach him every day with all kinds of collaboration proposals.
“You are the first person who can talk to me like this,” he told me. “Others only think about money.”
Of course money matters. But for him, money only matters because he wants the world to truly respect and be in awe of the wisdom system of Chinese civilization. I was glad he finally had a listener. I also felt his refusal to accept that this civilization should remain misunderstood or underestimated.
What he needs is a community of people who hold real love, curiosity, and reverence for this culture. And honestly, isn’t this exactly what I have always wanted to build?
Also, I personally have an almost supreme longing for Eastern metaphysics. Compared with the Kabbalistic system, it feels so elegant, restrained, and profound.
So I am making this open call for him here:
If you also want to see us turn this into one of the biggest new-era mystical IPs, and help bring it to the world with the scale and reverence it deserves, please DM me.
Come witness it. Or even better, come be part of it.
